Shen Bao Local Supplement

Literature and Art

Miscellaneous Thoughts: Eight Poems 234

— Songfu

The general still guards the frontier, vowing not to return until Lou Lan is defeated. Submitting to ignoble survival is not his ambition; he will promptly revolt to protect the homeland.

The southern spirit is inherently strong; a lone army resists the Japanese for long. Utterly eliminate the hatred of national subjugation; dare to rely on iron and blood to assist the central government.

The flames of war rage in Zhabei; a calamitous disaster surpassing the Hong-Yang Rebellion. Books and culture are turned to scorched earth, no less than the Qin Emperor of old.

More than a month of stealing life from the tiger's mouth, fleeing in distress, unable to live in peace. Turning back, I gaze north with furrowed brows; the former prosperity is now ruins.

Airplanes buzz and circle at will; the fate of the nation is at stake. Hurriedly escaping the tiger's den at dawn, the whole family is startled and sleepless.

The sound of artillery fire fills the night with terror; the displaced people sadly live out their lives. Both north and south of the Shanghai River suffer calamity; the sound of the watchman's clapper is always heard.

Two months have passed since the ceasefire; the withdrawal of Japanese troops is still delayed. Although the League of Nations conference has concluded, this is the time to strive for a strong nation.

The institutions set up by the puppets are full of thorns; they extort from everyone, but who can they turn to? Their cries are no different from the Stone Moat official; the old woman goes out the door, tears streaming down.

Science

How Ice Cream is Made 235

— Baitao

In summer, ice cream has become our only wonderful product for escaping the heat. When the sultry heat is overwhelming, taking spoonful after spoonful with a silver spoon, or savoring it with your tongue, is the most enjoyable thing.

The texture of high-quality ice cream is exceptionally smooth. This smoothness depends on the proportions of the various ingredients and the freezing technique.

The usual method for mixing ice cream: 60 to 70 percent is water, with the rest being sugar, milk, coloring, and fat. The fat exists in small globules in the milk, which can only be seen with a microscope. The sugar is dissolved before being added. When freezing it, it must be frozen extremely finely and transparently; the finer the better. Therefore, we must put it in an ice cream maker and stir it vigorously until it tastes exceptionally smooth on your tongue.

To know whether these ingredients are well-mixed, just see if the ice cream has small air bubbles after mixing and stirring.

After the ice cream is made, it can be divided into thin slices, packed into paper boxes, and then sealed off from the air or put in the refrigerator.

You must vigorously beat air into the ice cream to give it viscosity, or add some cornstarch, gum, dried egg yolk, or eggs to the ingredients. These components account for a very small proportion.

Essays on Humor

One of the Arts of Running a School 236

— Yingdai

Private schools rely on tuition fees for their funding. Naturally, the more students, the better. But in Shanghai, private schools are everywhere, as numerous as carp crossing the river. If you don't understand the art of running a school, you are guaranteed to fail. Running a school has its art, which outsiders might not believe. But people running schools in Shanghai really must have the skills of a school-running artist.

First, let me talk about recruitment advertisements. These advertisements are not those placed in newspapers but those pasted on walls. Because during summer and winter vacations, schools in Shanghai use colorful advertisements pasted on the walls. With summer vacation approaching, the recruitment advertisements on the walls are increasing day by day.

"Pasting recruitment advertisements earlier than others will attract attention."

"If the school is registered, the words 'Registered with the Municipal Bureau of Education' must be placed on top of the advertisement. This way, no matter how bad the content is, people will think that your school must be very good to be registered."

"If there are famous people known to everyone on the board of directors, you must print their names on the advertisement."

"The characters used in the advertisement must be artistic. Dull characters will not attract attention. If there are slogans attached, add more exclamation points '!' for punctuation."

"The color of the paper and the color of the characters on the advertisement must also be appropriately matched to attract attention. Black characters on white paper are not as eye-catching as blue characters, so the color scheme must also be considered!"

"Using two-color or three-color printed recruitment advertisements, with the middle characters printed half red and half green, will of course be even more effective. This method can be widely adopted."

"When various schools successively recruit students, it is best to have someone post recruitment advertisements every day, because soon after you post them, someone will paste someone else's recruitment advertisement on top, covering yours."

"As for recruitment advertisements in newspapers, the position must be prominent, the space occupied must be large, the characters must be written specially, registration must also be indicated, more famous directors should be written about, and it should be published earlier and stopped later than others...If the principal and dean have doctoral or master's degrees, it can naturally also be printed."

How many schools are there in Shanghai? To win, you must compete, and recruitment advertising is one of the competitive weapons. Alas! The means of enthusiastic education are like this?

Startling

After a Ship Encounters Danger 237

— Mengyu

A few days ago, the French mail ship "Georges Philippar" caught fire in the Red Sea, and the river steamer "Yiling" ran aground and sank near Xuan Chang. Recently, it was discovered that the Shengjing, Xin Jiang Tian, and other ships were almost in danger. What terrible tragedies! What do you all think when you recall the chaotic scenes of all the people on board frantically escaping? But while passengers can escape, the crew must still carry out rescue measures. Perhaps you don't know the emergency work of the crew at this time. I used to serve on a German merchant ship and personally encountered such a danger. Now, I will write down the situation at the time for you to see.

Our ship was a cargo ship without passengers. On the night of December 1, 1929, it accidentally hit a reef on Dongsha Island, and three large holes were broken in the bottom of the ship. Sea water poured in like a fountain. The situation was extremely dangerous at the time. Fortunately, it was not far from a shoal, so the captain immediately increased speed and steered towards the shoal while summoning the crew. Everyone quickly put on life jackets and began rescue work. Rescue efforts were roughly divided into the following types:

(1) Transmitting the distress call SOS by radio;

(2) Firing distress rockets (these rockets are made of thick bamboo, filled with gunpowder. When fired, they rise dozens of feet, and ships within ten miles can see them. They are actually the same as the "moon cannons" played with during the New Year, but bigger); If it is daytime, then instead of firing rockets, distress flags are raised;

(3) Continuously sounding the foghorn, about once every ten seconds.

There were also self-rescue methods:

(1) The sailors put the lifeboats into the water beside the ship so that they could escape into the boats when the big ship sank;

(2) Using extremely large pumps in the bottom of the ship to pump out the water entering through the broken holes.

In the end, the radio reached the Little Luzon coastal radio station, which sent a warship to rescue us from danger. No one was killed or injured, but because the navigation rules stipulate "rescuing people, not objects," everyone's luggage and clothes were lost.

After we safely reached the shore, the captain said to me: "Everyone ideally thinks that after a big ship sinks, they can rely on lifeboats and life jackets. In reality, ships sink too quickly at sea, and if other ships don't arrive in time to rescue, then passengers and crew will inevitably lose their lives. Imagine that a ship in distress is blown by the wind and tossed by the waves, unable to control itself, leading to this misfortune. Can lifeboats withstand such great winds and waves? Wearing a life jacket and floating on the water is even more useless, because the seawater is very cold and the waves are high. People who can swim might be able to last for a quarter of an hour; people who can't swim will die in five minutes. This method is indeed effective in small rivers."
